Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\\n54: // functionality described in the \\\"Assignment to a Queue\\\", \\\"Queuing\\\",\\n55: // and \\\"Dispatching\\\" sections of\\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\\n58: // today is not that day.\\n59: type QueueSet interface {\\n60: \\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\\n61: \\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\\n62: \\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\\n63: \\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\\n64: \\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\\n65: \\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\\n66: \\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\\n67: \\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\\n68: \\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n69: \\n70: \\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\\n71: \\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\\n72: \\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n79: \\t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\\n80: \\t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\\n81: \\t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\\n82: \\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\\n83: \\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\\n84: \\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\\n85: \\t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\\n86: \\t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\\n87: \\t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\\n88: \\t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\\n89: \\t// exactly once.\\n90: \\tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\\n91: \\n92: \\t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\\n93: \\t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\\n94: \\t// any requests.\\n95: \\t// For debugging only.\\n96: \\tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\\n101: \\n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\\n103: type Request interface {\\n104: \\t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\\n105: \\t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\\n106: \\t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\\n107: \\t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\\n108: \\t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\\n109: \\tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\\n114: \\t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\\n115: \\tName string\\n116: \\n117: \\t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\\n118: \\t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\\n119: \\t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\\n120: \\t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\\n121: \\t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\\n122: \\t// (i.e., the requests are \\\"exempt\\\" from limitation).\\n123: \\tDesiredNumQueues int\\n124: \\n125: \\t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\\n126: \\tQueueLengthLimit int\\n127: \\n128: \\t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\\n129: \\t// dealing a \\\"hand\\\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\\n130: \\tHandSize int\\n131: }\\n132: \\n133: // DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\\n134: type DispatchingConfig struct {\\n135: \\t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\\n136: \\tConcurrencyLimit int\\n137: \\n138: \\t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\\n139: \\t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\\n140: \\tConcurrencyDenominator int\\n141: }\\n142: Otherwise idle==false\\n88: \\t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\\n89: \\t// exactly once.\\n90: \\tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\\n91: \\n92: \\t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\\n93: \\t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\\n94: \\t// any requests.\\n95: \\t// For debugging only.\\n96: \\tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\\n101: \\n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\\n103: type Request interface {\\n104: \\t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\\n105: \\t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\\n106: \\t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\\n107: \\t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\\n108: \\t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\\n109: \\tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\\n114: \\t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\\n115: \\tName string\\n116: \\n117: \\t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\\n118: \\t// should exist now. Creation, like\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\n33: \t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\n34: \t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\n35: \t// execution covering just the regular phase.\n36: \t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\n37: \t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\n38: \t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\n39: \t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\n40: \t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\n41: \tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n42: }\n43: \n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\n47: \t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\n48: \t// dispatching configuration.\n49: \tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n50: }\n51: \n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\n54: // functionality described in the \"Assignment to a Queue\", \"Queuing\",\n55: // and \"Dispatching\" sections of\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\n58: // today is not that day.\n59: type QueueSet interface {\n60: \t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\n61: \t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\n62: \t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\n63: \t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\n64: \t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\n65: \t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\n66: \t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\n67: \t// and until it is undesired and empty.\n68: \tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n69: \n70: \t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\n71: \t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\n72: \t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\n73: \t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\n74: \t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\n75: \t// from false to true.\n76: \tIsIdle() bool\n77: \n78: \t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\n79: \t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\n80: \t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\n81: \t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\n82: \t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\n83: \t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\n84: \t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\n85: \t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\n86: \t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\n87: \t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\n88: \t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\n89: \t// exactly once.\n90: \tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\n91: \n92: \t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\n93: \t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\n94: \t// any requests.\n95: \t// For debugging only.\n96: \tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n97: }\n98: \n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n101: \n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\n103: type Request interface {\n104: \t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\n105: \t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\n106: \t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\n107: \t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\n108: \t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\n109: \tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\n110: }\n111: \n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\n114: \t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\n115: \tName string\n116: \n117: \t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\n118: \t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\n119: \t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\n120: \t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\n121: \t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\n122: \t// (i.e., the requests are \"exempt\" from limitation).\n123: \tDesiredNumQueues int\n124: \n125: \t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\n126: \tQueueLengthLimit int\n127: \n128: \t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\n129: \t// dealing a \"hand\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\n130: \tHandSize int\n131: }\n132: \n133: // DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\n134: type DispatchingConfig struct {\n135: \t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\n136: \tConcurrencyLimit int\n137: \n138: \t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\n139: \t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\n140: \tConcurrencyDenominator int\n141: }\n142: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01EmNm1cy8JoqFnj5yF9MCkA","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package queueset implements a technique called \\\"fair queuing for\\n18: // server requests\\\".  One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\\n19: // according to this technique.\\n20: //\\n21: // Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\\n22: // technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\\n27: //\\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\\n33: // completes.\\n34: //\\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \\\"R(t)\\\" in the original paper and\\n37: // \\\"virtual time\\\" in the implementation outline. In that\\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \\\"R(t)\\\" is the\\n40: // number of \\\"rounds\\\" that have been completed at real time t ---\\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \\\"in\\\" its queue until the\\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\\n53: // respect to t is\\n54: //\\n55: //\\t1 / NEQ(t) .\\n56: //\\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\\n59: //\\n60: //\\tC / NEQ(t) .\\n61: //\\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \\\"q\\\", let us also write \\\"reqs(q, t)\\\" for\\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\\n72: //\\n73: //\\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\\n74: //\\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\\n80: //\\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\\n85: // not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper’s adjustment by\\n86: // `$\\\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\\n87: //\\n88: // For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\\n89: // initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\\n90: // G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\\n91: // minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\\n92: // but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\\n93: // long-term behavior.\\n94: //\\n95: // As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\\n96: // the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\\n97: // version it is C requests.\\n98: //\\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\\n109: // to the current virtual time. The virtual finish time of request\\n110: // number J in the queue (counting from J=1 for the head) is J * G +\\n111: // (queue's virtual start time). While the queue is non-empty: the\\n112: // last virtual finish time of the queue is the virtual finish time of\\n113: // the last request in the queue. While the queue is empty and has a\\n114: // request executing: the last virtual finish time is the queue’s\\n115: // virtual start time. When a request is dequeued for service the\\n116: // queue’s virtual start time is advanced by G. When a request\\n117: // finishes being served, and the actual service time was S, the\\n118: // queue’s virtual start time is decremented by G - S.\\n119: package queueset\\n120: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"846efc90-d2a8-4ef1-9026-4f3db0698869","uuid":"b151d6a4-40a0-4285-9220-4c4af6c75dd2","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package queueset implements a technique called \\\"fair queuing for\\n18: // server requests\\\". For our problem, we can define a\\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\\n53: // respect to t is\\n54: //\\n55: //\\t1 / NEQ(t) .\\n56: //\\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\\n59: //\\n60: //\\tC / NEQ(t) .\\n61: //\\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \\\"q\\\", let us also write \\\"reqs(q, t)\\\" for\\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\\n72: //\\n73: //\\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\\n74: //\\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\\n80: //\\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\\n85: // not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper’s adjustment by\\n86: // `$\\\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\\n87: //\\n88: // For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\\n89: // initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\\n90: // G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\\n91: // minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\\n92: // but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\\n93: // long-term behavior.\\n94: //\\n95: // As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\\n96: // the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\\n97: // version it is C requests.\\n98: //\\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\\n109: // to the current virtual time. The virtual finish time of request\\n110: // number J in the queue (counting from J=1 for the head) is J * G +\\n111: // (queue's virtual start time). While the queue is non-empty: the\\n112: // last virtual finish time of the queue is the virtual finish time of\\n113: // the last request in the queue. While the queue is empty and has a\\n114: // request executing: the last virtual finish time is the queue’s\\n115: // virtual start time. When a request is dequeued for service the\\n116: // queue’s virtual start time is advanced by G. When a request\\n117: // finishes being served, and the actual service time was S, the\\n118: // queue’s virtual start time is decremented by G - S.\\n119: package queueset\\n120: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /*\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package queueset implements a technique called \"fair queuing for\n18: // server requests\".  One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\n19: // according to this technique.\n20: //\n21: // Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\n22: // technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\n27: //\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\n33: // completes.\n34: //\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \"R(t)\" in the original paper and\n37: // \"virtual time\" in the implementation outline. In that\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \"R(t)\" is the\n40: // number of \"rounds\" that have been completed at real time t ---\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \"in\" its queue until the\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\n53: // respect to t is\n54: //\n55: //\t1 / NEQ(t) .\n56: //\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\n59: //\n60: //\tC / NEQ(t) .\n61: //\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \"q\", let us also write \"reqs(q, t)\" for\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\n72: //\n73: //\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\n74: //\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\n80: //\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\n85: // not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper’s adjustment by\n86: // `$\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\n87: //\n88: // For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\n89: // initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\n90: // G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\n91: // minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\n92: // but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\n93: // long-term behavior.\n94: //\n95: // As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\n96: // the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\n97: // version it is C requests.\n98: //\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\n109: // to the current virtual time. The virtual finish time of request\n110: // number J in the queue (counting from J=1 for the head) is J * G +\n111: // (queue's virtual start time). While the queue is non-empty: the\n112: // last virtual finish time of the queue is the virtual finish time of\n113: // the last request in the queue. While the queue is empty and has a\n114: // request executing: the last virtual finish time is the queue’s\n115: // virtual start time. When a request is dequeued for service the\n116: // queue’s virtual start time is advanced by G. When a request\n117: // finishes being served, and the actual service time was S, the\n118: // queue’s virtual start time is decremented by G - S.\n119: package queueset\n120: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go"}}}

The fields listed before the lock\\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\\n73: //\\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\\n75: // suffix \\\"Locked\\\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\\n76: // whose name does not end in \\\"Locked\\\" either acquires the lock or\\n77: // does not care about locking.\\n78: //\\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\\n80: // \\\"ToBoundLocked\\\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`.  This is so for a method that\\n82: // changes what request is oldest in a queue, because that change means\\n83: // that the anti-windup hack in boundNextDispatchLocked needs to be\\n84: // applied wrt the revised oldest request in the queue.\\n85: type queueSet struct {\\n86: \\tclock                    eventclock.Interface\\n87: \\testimatedServiceDuration time.Duration\\n88: \\n89: \\treqsGaugePair metrics.RatioedGaugePair // .RequestsExecuting covers regular phase only\\n90: \\n91: \\texecSeatsGauge metrics.RatioedGauge // for all phases of execution\\n92: \\n93: \\tseatDemandIntegrator metrics.Gauge\\n94: \\n95: \\tpromiseFactory promiseFactory\\n96: \\n97: \\tlock sync.Mutex\\n98: \\n99: \\t// qCfg holds the current queuing configuration. }\\n229: \\n230: // createQueues is a helper method for initializing an array of n queues\\n231: func createQueues(n, baseIndex int) []*queue {\\n232: \\tfqqueues := make([]*queue, n)\\n233: \\tfor i }\\n238: \\n239: func (qs *queueSet) BeginConfigChange(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig) (fq.QueueSetCompleter, error) {\\n240: \\tdealer, err := checkConfig(qCfg)\\n241: \\tif err != nil {\\n242: \\t\\treturn Call this after getting a\n1084: // clue that the given priority level is undesired and idle.\n1085: func (cfgCtlr *configController) maybeReap(plName string) {\n1086: \tcfgCtlr.lock.RLock()\n1087: \tdefer cfgCtlr.lock.RUnlock()\n1088: \tplState := cfgCtlr.priorityLevelStates[plName]\n1089: \tif plState == nil {\n1090: \t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"plName=%s, plState==nil\", plName)\n1091: \t\treturn\n1092: \t}\n1093: \tuseless := plState.quiescing && plState.numPending == 0 && plState.queues.IsIdle()\n1094: \tklog.V(7).Infof(\"plState.quiescing=%v, plState.numPending=%d, useless=%v\", plState.quiescing, plState.numPending, useless)\n1095: \tif !useless {\n1096: \t\treturn\n1097: \t}\n1098: \tklog.V(3).Infof(\"Triggered API priority and fairness config reloading because priority level %s is undesired and idle\", plName)\n1099: \tcfgCtlr.configQueue.Add(0)\n1100: }\n1101: \n1102: // maybeReapLocked requires the cfgCtlr's lock to already be held and\n1103: // will remove the last internal traces of the named priority level if\n1104: // it has no more use. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018HaU1jSmvV74T3tkPtvRUt","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_0128G6qKSE9tpATq7G7FiFwN","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# APF QueueSet Subsystem: Deep-Dive Analysis\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Advanced Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem implements fair queuing for server requests in the Kubernetes API server. It provides isolation and prioritization across multiple request flows by managing queues with virtual time-based scheduling and shuffle-sharded queue selection. This document analyzes the architecture, algorithms, data flow, and operational characteristics of this critical subsystem.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem ensures fair and prioritized execution of API server requests by:\n\n1. **Preventing resource starvation**: Multiple flow classes (defined by flow schemas and flow distinguishers) share concurrency fairly\n2. **Enforcing concurrency limits**: Ensuring total executing requests don't exceed server capacity\n3. **Fair queueing**: When requests must wait, they're dispatched in a fair manner proportional to flow class share\n4. **Queue isolation**: Using shuffle sharding to reduce head-of-line blocking across unrelated flows\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n- **APF Controller** (`apf_controller.go`): Manages configuration, FlowSchema/PriorityLevel matching, and concurrency allocation\n- **Flow Control Filter** (`apf_filter.go`): HTTP filter layer that invokes Handle() for each request\n- **Request metadata**: RequestInfo, User, authentication information from request context\n- **Concurrency allocation** (`conc_alloc.go`): Computes fair concurrency distributions across priority levels\n- **Event Clock** (`fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time advancement for the fair queuing algorithm\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n\n- **Request execution**: The filter decides whether to execute, queue, or reject each request\n- **Metrics** (`metrics/`): Reports request counts, seat usage, queue depths, virtual time progression\n- **Watch tracking**: For long-running watch requests with extended latency characteristics\n\n### Boundary Definition\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem is responsible for:\n- ✅ Queueing decisions for a single priority level\n- ✅ Virtual time calculation and dispatch ordering\n- ✅ Shuffle sharding for queue selection\n- ✅ Tracking executing request seats and work durations\n\nThe QueueSet is NOT responsible for:\n- ❌ FlowSchema/PriorityLevel matching (controller)\n- ❌ Concurrency limit calculation (controller via concurrency allocation)\n- ❌ Configuration updates (controller)\n- ❌ Final rejection vs. retry decisions (client-side)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Data Structures\n\n#### `queueSet` (primary coordinator)\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\nCoordinates all queuing and dispatching logic for a single priority level:\n\n| Field | Responsibility |\n|-------|-----------------|\n| `queues []*queue` | Array of FIFO queues, one per shuffle-shard |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Virtual time (progress meter) in units of \"seat-seconds\" |\n| `lastRealTime time.Time` | Timestamp of last virtual time update |\n| `robinIndex int` | Round-robin cursor for fair queue selection |\n| `dCfg DispatchingConfig` | Concurrency limit and denominator for metrics |\n| `qCfg QueuingConfig` | Number of queues, queue length limits |\n| `dealer Dealer` | Shuffle sharding dealer for queue selection |\n| `totRequestsWaiting/Executing` | Counters for active requests |\n| `totSeatsInUse/Waiting` | Counters for multi-seat requests |\n\n**Key responsibility**: Maintains virtual time state, selects queues, makes dispatch decisions.\n\n#### `queue` (per-shard FIFO)\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\nRepresents one FIFO queue within the queueSet:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `requestsWaiting fifo` | Waiting requests in FIFO order |\n| `requestsExecuting set[*request]` | Currently executing requests from this queue |\n| `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds` | Virtual start time for this queue; advances by total work of dispatched requests |\n| `seatsInUse int` | Seats occupied by executing requests |\n| `index int` | Position in the queueSet's queue array |\n\n**Key responsibility**: Stores and manages requests for one flow shard, tracks virtual dispatch point.\n\n#### `request` (request wrapper)\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\nTemporary container wrapping application-level requests with APF metadata:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `arrivalTime, arrivalR` | Real and virtual time at arrival |\n| `startTime` | When dispatch/execution began |\n| `decision promise.WriteOnce` | Outcome: execute, cancel, or reject (set once) |\n| `workEstimate` | InitialSeats (execution phase), FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency |\n| `queue *queue` | Owning queue (nil if no queueing) |\n| `ctx context.Context` | Request context (may be canceled) |\n\n**Key responsibility**: Carries per-request state through the queueing pipeline.\n\n#### `completedWorkEstimate`\nWork estimate including computed totals:\n\n```go\ntype completedWorkEstimate struct {\n    WorkEstimate\n    totalWork fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // initial + final work\n    finalWork fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // only final work\n}\n```\n\nComputed as:\n- `initialWork = InitialSeats × estimatedServiceDuration`\n- `finalWork = FinalSeats × AdditionalLatency`\n- `totalWork = initialWork + finalWork`\n\n### 2.2 Execution Paths and Responsibility Boundaries\n\n#### Path 1: Exempt (no queueing)\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues < 0`:\n- Request immediately proceeds to execution\n- No queue selection, no virtual time update\n- No seat accounting (user bears risk)\n\n#### Path 2: No queuing (direct concurrency limit)\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues == 0`:\n- Check if request fits within remaining `ConcurrencyLimit`\n- If no: reject immediately\n- If yes: execute directly (no FIFO queue)\n- Still tracks seats and executing count\n\n#### Path 3: Full queuing (shuffle-sharded)\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues > 0`:\n1. **Shuffle shard**: Select queue using flow distinguisher hash\n2. **Enqueue or reject**: If at max queue length AND at concurrency limit, reject\n3. **Dispatch loop**: Dequeue requests in virtual time order\n4. **Track seats**: Monitor multi-seat requests in execution phase\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\n### 3.1 Inbound Request: Arrival Phase\n\n**Entry point**: `apf_filter.go:155-198` - `Handle()` method\n\n```\nHTTP Request\n    ↓\n[APF Filter] Handle() entry\n    ↓ (calls)\nstartRequest() [apf_controller.go:1022-1079]\n    ├─ Match FlowSchema (line 1031-1052)\n    ├─ Lookup PriorityLevelConfiguration (line 1053-1066)\n    ├─ Compute flow distinguisher if needed (line 1063)\n    ├─ Call workEstimator() to get InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency\n    └─ Call plState.queues.StartRequest()\n```\n\n**Example code** (`apf_controller.go:1075`):\n```go\nreq, idle := plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue,\n    flowDistinguisher, selectedFlowSchema.Name, rd.RequestInfo, rd.User, queueNoteFn)\n```\n\n### 3.2 QueueSet Entry: Request Classification\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:308-356` - `StartRequest()`\n\n```\nStartRequest() entry\n    ↓\n[Step 0: Check if queueing disabled]\nIf DesiredNumQueues < 1 (line 316):\n    ├─ Check canAccommodateSeats() (line 317)\n    ├─ If no: reject, return nil (line 322)\n    └─ If yes: dispatchSansQueueLocked() → execute immediately\n\n[Step 1: Queue selection and enqueue]\nElse:\n    ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked() (line 334)\n    │   ├─ Shuffle shard to select queue (line 554)\n    │   ├─ Create request struct (line 560-573)\n    │   ├─ Check queue length + concurrency limits (rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked, line 618-629)\n    │   └─ Enqueue to FIFO if not full (enqueueToBoundLocked, line 632-651)\n    │       └─ Initialize queue.nextDispatchR = currentR if first request (line 637)\n    ├─ If enqueue failed: return nil (line 337-341)\n    │\n[Step 2: Dispatch loop]\n    └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() (line 353)\n        └─ Loop: while waiting requests AND seats available:\n            └─ dispatchLocked() (line 695-743)\n```\n\n### 3.3 Queue Selection: Shuffle Sharding\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:583-612` - `shuffleShardLocked()`\n\nThe shuffle sharding algorithm selects one queue from a \"hand\" of candidates:\n\n```\nInput: hashValue (derived from flow schema name + distinguisher)\n\n1. dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backhand[8]) (line 587)\n   └─ Returns array of 8 queue indices, dealt from 52-card deck of queues\n\n2. Find queue with minimum total work (line 593-606):\n   for i in handSize:\n       queueIdx := hand[(offset + i) % handSize]\n       thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n       if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds:\n           bestQueueIdx := queueIdx\n\n3. Return bestQueueIdx\n```\n\n**Fairness property**: Each flow hash is dealt the same hand size (8 by default). One \"bad\" flow (with many requests) gets at most one of the 8 candidate queues, leaving 7 for other flows.\n\n**Code evidence** (`queueset.go:596-605`):\n```go\n// Select queue with minimum total work among the hand\nfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n    queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n    queue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n    queueSum := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum()\n\n    thisQueueSeatSeconds := queueSum.TotalWorkSum  // Total work metric\n    if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n        minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.4 Virtual Time Management\n\n**Core mechanism**: Virtual time (`currentR`) advances at a rate proportional to available concurrency and number of active queues.\n\n#### Rate Calculation\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:526-541` - `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n    activeQueues := 0\n    seatsRequested := 0\n\n    for _, queue := range qs.queues {\n        // Sum seats needed by executing + waiting requests\n        seatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n            activeQueues++\n        }\n    }\n\n    if activeQueues == 0 {\n        return 0  // No work in progress\n    }\n\n    // Rate = min(available seats, concurrency limit) / active queues\n    return math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n}\n```\n\n#### Time Sync\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:461-479` - `syncTimeLocked()`\n\nCalled on every lock acquisition. Updates `currentR` based on elapsed real time:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    qs.lastRealTime = realNow\n\n    prevR := qs.currentR\n    incrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n\n    // Epoch advance to prevent overflow (when R > highR threshold)\n    if qs.currentR >= highR {\n        qs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.5 Dispatching: Virtual Time Ordering\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:695-743` - `dispatchLocked()`\n\nSelects the next request to execute based on virtual finish time:\n\n```\n1. findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked() (line 696) [queueset.go:776-843]:\n\n   For each queue (in round-robin order):\n       oldestReq := peek at FIFO head\n       if oldestReq != nil:\n           // Virtual finish time = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestReq.totalWork()\n           virtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestReq.totalWork()\n           if virtualFinish < minVirtualFinish:\n               minQueue := queue\n               minVirtualFinish := virtualFinish\n\n   Return minQueue and its oldest request\n\n2. Validate dispatch (line 811):\n   canAccommodateSeats(oldestReq.MaxSeats())\n   └─ Check if request fits within remaining concurrency limit\n\n3. Adjust finalWork (line 827-832):\n   If FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit:\n       Reduce FinalSeats to ConcurrencyLimit\n       Scale AdditionalLatency to preserve total work\n\n4. Update virtual time (line 741):\n   queue.nextDispatchR += oldestReq.totalWork()\n   └─ Queue advances by total work of dispatched request\n\n5. Track execution (line 720-728):\n   totRequestsExecuting++\n   totSeatsInUse += oldestReq.MaxSeats()\n   queue.requestsExecuting.insert(oldestReq)\n   queue.seatsInUse += oldestReq.MaxSeats()\n```\n\n**Fairness property**: Virtual finish time = next-dispatch-point + request-work. Queues with less work waiting get dispatched sooner, ensuring fairness.\n\n**Code evidence** (`queueset.go:795-801`):\n```go\ncurrentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\nif currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n    minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n    minQueue = queue\n    minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n}\n```\n\n### 3.6 Request Execution and Finish\n\n**Method**: `apf_filter.go:179-193` - `req.Finish()` in Handle()\n\n```\nreq.Finish(execFn) → req.wait() in queueset.go:397-441\n    ├─ Get decision from promise (line 404)\n    │   └─ Blocks until decision is set (during dispatch)\n    │\n    └─ Switch on decision (line 414-422):\n        ├─ decisionExecute: call execFn() and proceed\n        ├─ decisionCancel/timeout: remove from queue, reject\n\nfinishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req) [queueset.go:851-858]\n    ├─ finishRequestLocked(req) (line 855)\n    │   ├─ Update virtual time: queue.nextDispatchR -= (G - S) × width\n    │   │   (G = estimatedServiceDuration, S = actual service time)\n    │   ├─ Handle multi-phase requests:\n    │   │   If AdditionalLatency > 0:\n    │   │       Schedule deferred release via clock.EventAfterDuration()\n    │   │   Else:\n    │   │       Release seats immediately\n    │   └─ removeQueueIfEmptyLocked(req)\n    │       └─ Remove queue if excess and now empty\n    │\n    └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() (line 856)\n        └─ Continue dispatching waiting requests\n```\n\n**Important detail**: Virtual time adjustment (line 938) handles the case where actual service time differs from estimate:\n\n```go\n// When a request finishes being served, and the actual service time was S,\n// the queue's start R is decremented by (G - S)*width.\nr.queue.nextDispatchR -= fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(\n    float64(r.InitialSeats()),\n    qs.estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration,\n)\n```\n\nIf a request ran faster than expected, we credit back virtual time to help that queue. This ensures estimates don't permanently skew fairness.\n\n### 3.7 Complete Request Lifecycle Example\n\n```\nTime=0: Request arrives\n├─ FlowSchema matched: \"user-flows\" with flow distinguisher \"alice\"\n├─ PriorityLevel: \"standard\" (limit=100, queues=10)\n├─ WorkEstimate: InitialSeats=2, FinalSeats=1, AdditionalLatency=10ms\n\nT=0+: shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n├─ hash = sha256([\"user-flows\", \"alice\"])\n├─ dealer.DealIntoHand(hash) → [3, 7, 1, 5, ...]\n├─ Evaluate: queue[3].work=50, queue[7].work=20, queue[1].work=60, queue[5].work=15\n├─ Select: queue[5] (minimum work=15)\n└─ Enqueue: request added to queue[5].requestsWaiting\n\nT=10ms: Virtual time advances\n├─ 3 active queues, 15 seats requested, 100-seat limit\n├─ Rate = min(15, 100) / 3 = 5 seat-seconds/real-second\n├─ incrR = 5 × 0.01s = 0.05 seat-seconds\n└─ currentR = 0 + 0.05 = 0.05\n\nT=15ms: dispatchLocked() checks all queues\n├─ queue[0]: oldestReq.work=10, virtualFinish = 0.0 + 10 = 10.0\n├─ queue[5]: oldestReq.work=3, virtualFinish = 0.05 + 3 = 3.05  ← Minimum\n└─ Dispatch request from queue[5]\n    ├─ queue[5].nextDispatchR = 0.05 + 3.0 = 3.05\n    ├─ totRequestsExecuting++\n    ├─ totSeatsInUse += 2\n\nT=25ms: Request execution completes\n├─ actualServiceTime = 25 - 15 = 10ms\n├─ Adjustment: queue[5].nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(2, 3ms - 10ms)\n│  = SeatsTimesDuration(2, -7ms) = 2 × (-0.007) = -0.014\n├─ queue[5].nextDispatchR = 3.05 - 0.014 = 3.036 (credited back)\n└─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() tries to dispatch next request\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fair Queuing Algorithm and Virtual Time Mechanism\n\n### 4.1 Algorithm Foundations\n\nThe implementation is based on **Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ)** adapted for server requests, documented in the original research paper on fair queuing and explained in depth in `doc.go`.\n\n**Key adaptation**: Instead of transmitting one packet at a time from one queue, the algorithm:\n1. Dispatches multiple requests concurrently (up to `ConcurrencyLimit`)\n2. Weights by request \"width\" (seats) instead of packet size\n3. Estimates service time rather than measuring packet transmission\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Formula\n\nIn traditional fair queuing, virtual time advances as:\n\n```\ndR/dt = 1 / NEQ(t)\n\nwhere NEQ(t) = number of non-empty queues\n```\n\nFor concurrent server requests with C concurrency limit:\n\n```\ndR/dt = min(C, sum of reqs(q, t)) / NEQ(t)\n\nwhere reqs(q, t) = number of requests executing from queue q\n```\n\n**Implementation** (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked`):\n\n```go\nreturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n```\n\n### 4.3 Virtual Finish Time\n\nVirtual finish time for a request in queue q:\n\n```\nVFT_i = queue.nextDispatchR + (work of request i)\n\nwhere work = InitialSeats × EstimatedServiceDuration + FinalSeats × AdditionalLatency\n```\n\nThe request with the **minimum virtual finish time** across all queues is dispatched next.\n\n**Invariant**: This ensures each queue makes proportional progress, and requests are served fairly.\n\n### 4.4 Virtual Start Time and Anti-Windup\n\nTo avoid expensive computation of virtual finish times for each request, the implementation uses virtual start time:\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR = virtual start time of next request\n\nRequest i's virtual finish time = queue.nextDispatchR + request[i].work\n```\n\nWhen a request finishes:\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.work  (at dispatch time)\n```\n\n**Anti-windup adjustment** (`boundNextDispatchLocked`, line 945-964):\n\nSome queues may be unable to use all allocated virtual time (e.g., queue with small requests competing for limited max-seats). Without correction, such queues would accumulate progressively earlier virtual start times, starving other queues.\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) boundNextDispatchLocked(queue *queue) {\n    oldestReq, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestReq == nil {\n        return\n    }\n    // Ensure virtual time doesn't precede arrival of next request\n    virtualStartBound = oldestReq.arrivalR\n    if queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n        queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis hack ensures dispatch in virtual time never precedes arrival in virtual time, preventing unfair accumulation of virtual time debt.\n\n### 4.5 Epoch Advancement (Overflow Handling)\n\n**Problem**: After long running, `currentR` can exceed the maximum SeatSeconds value.\n\n**Solution**: Periodically wind back all R values by `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds / 2` (line 483-522).\n\n```go\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement\n\n    for qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n        // Empty queues reset to zero\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n            queue.nextDispatchR = 0\n            continue\n        }\n        // Non-empty queues decrement by rDecrement\n        queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n\n        // Walk all waiting requests and decrement their arrivalR\n        queue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n            req.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n            return true\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Multi-Seat Requests and Work Estimation\n\n### 5.1 Seat Counting\n\nRequests can occupy multiple \"seats\" in the concurrency limit:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimate struct {\n    InitialSeats uint64  // Seats during main execution phase\n    FinalSeats uint64    // Seats during additional latency phase\n    AdditionalLatency time.Duration  // How long FinalSeats are held\n}\n```\n\n**Example**: A watch request might:\n- Occupy 1 InitialSeat for its response writing (fast)\n- Occupy 1 FinalSeat for 10 seconds of keep-alive streaming\n\n```\nReal time:  [==execute==][========streaming========]\nSeats:      1          1 (just FinalSeats)\n```\n\n### 5.2 Work Calculation\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:131-146`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) completeWorkEstimate(we *fcrequest.WorkEstimate) completedWorkEstimate {\n    finalWork := qs.computeFinalWork(we)\n    return completedWorkEstimate{\n        WorkEstimate: *we,\n        totalWork: qs.computeInitialWork(we) + finalWork,\n        finalWork: finalWork,\n    }\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) computeInitialWork(we *fcrequest.WorkEstimate) fcrequest.SeatSeconds {\n    return fcrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(float64(we.InitialSeats), qs.estimatedServiceDuration)\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) computeFinalWork(we *fcrequest.WorkEstimate) fcrequest.SeatSeconds {\n    return fcrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(float64(we.FinalSeats), we.AdditionalLatency)\n}\n```\n\n**Example calculation**:\n- InitialSeats = 2, FinalSeats = 1\n- EstimatedServiceDuration = 3ms (default)\n- AdditionalLatency = 10ms\n\n```\ninitialWork = 2 × 3ms = 6ms\nfinalWork = 1 × 10ms = 10ms\ntotalWork = 16ms\n```\n\nThis request's virtual finish time contribution: 16ms of seat-seconds.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 6.1 Rejection Scenarios\n\n#### Concurrency Limit Exceeded\n**Condition**: `totSeatsInUse >= dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` (line 622)\n\n**Action**: Reject if queue is also at length limit (line 622-625)\n\n```go\nif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n   curQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n    return false  // Reject\n}\n```\n\n**Metric**: `metrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"queue-full\")`\n\n#### Request Exceeds Per-Queue Limit\n**Limit**: `QueueLengthLimit` per queue (line 623)\n\n**When triggered**: Too many requests backed up in one shuffle shard\n\n**Action**: Reject new arrivals if limit reached AND concurrency limit also reached\n\n#### Large Single-Request Handling\n**Special case** (`canAccommodateSeatsLocked`, line 753-763):\n\nIf a request asks for more seats than the entire `ConcurrencyLimit`:\n\n```go\ncase seats > qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit:\n    if qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0 {\n        // Allow if no competition\n        return true\n    }\n    // Wait for all currently executing to finish\n    return false\n```\n\n**Tradeoff**: Allows oversized requests when system is idle, but blocks them when busy. Prevents deadlock where an oversized request can never be dispatched.\n\n### 6.2 Timeout Handling\n\n**Context cancellation** (`queueset.go:397-441` - `request.wait()`):\n\n```\nWhen req.decision.Get() returns:\n    ├─ decisionExecute: proceed to execution\n    └─ Other (cancel): remove from queue and reject\n        ├─ Decrement totRequestsWaiting and totSeatsWaiting\n        ├─ Increment totRequestsCancelled\n        └─ Emit metric: \"time-out\"\n```\n\nThe request decision is set by dispatching via `decision.Set(decisionExecute)` (line 710). If the context is cancelled before this, the request remains with its initial decision value (typically `decisionCancel`), causing it to be rejected.\n\n**Code evidence** (`queueset.go:565`):\n```go\ndecision: qs.promiseFactory(nil, ctx, decisionCancel),  // Default decision is cancel\n```\n\n### 6.3 Performance Limits\n\n| Metric | Limit | Constraint |\n|--------|-------|-----------|\n| `DesiredNumQueues` | 128+ | Shuffle sharding dealer supports up to ~200 queues |\n| `QueueLengthLimit` | ~10k | Per-queue memory, total = limit × numQueues |\n| `HandSize` | 8 (default) | Shuffle sharding parameter |\n| `ConcurrencyLimit` | Server-wide | Per priority level, allocated by APF controller |\n\n### 6.4 Virtual Time Overflow Protection\n\n**Problem**: `currentR` (SeatSeconds) can grow unbounded.\n\n**Solution**: Epoch advancement at `highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2` threshold (line 475-476)\n\n```go\nif qs.currentR >= highR {\n    qs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n}\n```\n\n**Metric**: `metrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)`\n\n### 6.5 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Shuffle Sharding vs. Complexity\n\n**Benefit**: Reduces head-of-line blocking. One misbehaving flow (e.g., many requests) is isolated to at most 1/8 of queues.\n\n**Cost**: Requires hash computation and dealer construction\n\n**Decision**: Shuffle sharding enabled when `numQueues > 1`, disabled for `numQueues <= 1`\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Estimated vs. Actual Service Time\n\n**Problem**: Service time isn't known until request completes.\n\n**Solution**: Use fixed estimate (`estimatedServiceDuration = 3ms`, line 215) to guide dispatch decisions\n\n**Adjustment**: When request finishes, adjust virtual time by `(estimate - actual) × width` (line 938)\n\n**Tradeoff**:\n- Fast requests (< 3ms) credit back virtual time → queues making quick progress get higher priority\n- Slow requests (> 3ms) consume more virtual time → heavily penalize slow requests\n- Result: Fairness by actual work done, not by request count\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Multi-Phase Execution with Additional Latency\n\n**Use case**: Watch requests stream results over a long period\n\n**Implementation** (`finishRequestLocked`, line 886-930):\n```go\nif r.workEstimate.AdditionalLatency <= 0 {\n    // Single-phase: release seats immediately\n    releaseSeatsLocked()\n} else {\n    // Two-phase: release later\n    qs.clock.EventAfterDuration(func(_ time.Time) {\n        releaseSeatsLocked()\n    }, additionalLatency)\n}\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Avoids stalling concurrency for long-running streams\n\n**Cost**: Requires additional tracking and deferred cleanup\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Round-Robin Queue Selection for Dispatch\n\n**Problem**: Finding minimum virtual finish time requires checking all queues.\n\n**Solution** (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`, line 785-803):\n\n```go\nfor range qs.queues {\n    qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq\n    // Check this queue...\n}\n```\n\nIterate in round-robin order so burst of same-queue requests doesn't monopolize CPU.\n\n**Benefit**: O(n) per dispatch, but doesn't starve other work\n\n**Cost**: Slight fairness variation (a queue checked first each cycle gets slight advantage)\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 QueueSetFactory and Testability\n\n**Interface** (`fairqueuing/interface.go:32-42`):\n\n```go\ntype QueueSetFactory interface {\n    BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, ...) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n}\n\ntype QueueSetCompleter interface {\n    Complete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n}\n```\n\n**Hook 1: Clock Substitution**\n\n```go\ntype queueSetFactory struct {\n    clock eventclock.Interface\n    promiseFactoryFactory promiseFactoryFactory\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point**: Inject alternative clock implementation (eventclock.Real or test clock)\n\n**Use case**: Deterministic testing; advance virtual time without wall-clock delays\n\n**Evidence** (`apf_filter.go:94-106`):\n```go\nclk := eventclock.Real{}\nreturn NewTestable(TestableConfig{\n    Clock: clk,\n    QueueSetFactory: fqs.NewQueueSetFactory(clk),\n})\n```\n\n### 7.2 Promise Implementation Substitution\n\n**Hook 2: WriteOnce Promise Factory**\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n```\n\nDetermines how request decisions (execute/cancel/reject) are communicated.\n\n**Extension**: Custom promise implementations for:\n- Batch decision processing\n- Tracing and observability\n- Alternative synchronization primitives\n\n**Default** (`ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory`, line 358-362):\n```go\nfunc ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory(qs *queueSet) promiseFactory {\n    return promise.NewWriteOnce\n}\n```\n\n### 7.3 QueueNoteFn Callback\n\n**Hook 3: Queue Entry/Exit Notification**\n\n```go\ntype QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n```\n\nInvoked when request enters and leaves queue (line 375-379):\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) NoteQueued(inQueue bool) {\n    if req.queueNoteFn != nil {\n        req.queueNoteFn(inQueue)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Extension use cases**:\n- Track per-request queue time\n- Update request counters for dashboards\n- Implement custom queue depth alerts\n\n**Evidence** (`apf_controller.go:1075`):\n```go\nreq, idle := plState.queues.StartRequest(..., queueNoteFn)\n```\n\n### 7.4 Work Estimator Callback\n\n**Hook 4: Dynamic Work Estimation**\n\n```go\nworkEstimator func() fcrequest.WorkEstimate\n```\n\nCalled after FlowSchema matching to determine request's seat/latency profile (apf_controller.go:1069):\n\n```go\nworkEstimate := workEstimator()\n```\n\n**Extension use cases**:\n- Estimate seats based on actual request size\n- Use machine learning to predict execution time\n- Adjust estimates based on server load history\n\n**Risk**: Bad estimates degrade fairness; must correlate with actual execution time\n\n### 7.5 Configuration Reconfiguration Interface\n\n**Hook 5: Live Configuration Updates**\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) BeginConfigChange(qCfg QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n    └─ Complete(dCfg DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n```\n\nAllows changing queue count, queue length limit, concurrency limit without disruption.\n\n**Implementation** (`setConfiguration`, line 254-287):\n- New queues added immediately\n- Old excess queues drained by attrition\n- Configuration changes processed atomically under lock\n\n**Extension**: This is the hook the APF controller uses to apply new FlowControl API objects.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Implications and Reliability\n\n### 8.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Virtual Time Advancement Cost\n\n**Per-lock-acquisition cost** (`syncTimeLocked`, line 465-479):\n```\nO(1) arithmetic to compute rate\nO(1) to update currentR\nO(n) to advance epoch (if triggered, once every highR/incrR lock acquisitions)\n```\n\nFor typical loads:\n- `incrR` ≈ 10-100 ms of seat-seconds per lock\n- Epoch advance triggered every ~10^6 lock acquisitions\n- **Impact**: Negligible on modern CPUs\n\n#### Dispatch Selection Cost\n\n**Per dispatch** (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`, line 776-843):\n```\nO(num_queues) to find minimum virtual finish time\n```\n\n**Mitigation**: Round-robin iteration prevents starvation of CPU resources.\n\n**Impact**: For 10 queues, ~1 microsecond per dispatch on modern CPUs\n\n#### Shuffle Sharding Cost\n\n**Per enqueue** (`shuffleShardLocked`, line 583-612):\n```\nO(hand_size) to evaluate queue candidates (typically 8)\nO(hand_size) to sum queue work\n```\n\n**Impact**: Negligible; hand size is fixed and small\n\n### 8.2 Memory Usage\n\n**Per QueueSet**:\n- Fixed: ~2KB for struct fields\n- Per queue: ~200 bytes base + request storage\n- Per request in queue: ~500 bytes (request struct + list node)\n\n**Formula for queue memory**:\n```\nTotal ≈ numQueues × (200 + queueLengthLimit × 500) bytes\n```\n\n**Example**: 10 queues, 100 requests per queue:\n```\n≈ 10 × (200 + 100 × 500) = 500KB\n```\n\n**Limitation**: Must size QueueLengthLimit appropriately; unbounded queues cause OOM.\n\n### 8.3 Fairness and Starvation Prevention\n\n#### Guaranteed Progress Properties\n\n1. **No starvation of queues**: Round-robin dispatch selection (line 785-803) ensures all queues are considered regularly\n\n2. **No indefinite queueing**: With finite ConcurrencyLimit and positive dispatch rate, every queued request eventually executes or is cancelled by timeout\n\n3. **Proportional fairness**: Virtual finish time ordering ensures CPU-seconds/wall-clock-time ratio is proportional to `(totalWork / sum_of_all_totalWork)`\n\n#### Potential Fairness Violations\n\n1. **Bad work estimates**: If `workEstimate` is far from actual service time, VFT ordering may not reflect true fairness\n\n2. **Skewed request distributions**: Workload where one flow has many small requests vs. another with few large requests may see fairness violations if hand size is too small (unlikely with hand size=8)\n\n3. **Large single-request behavior**: A request asking for > ConcurrencyLimit seats blocks all other requests until system idle (line 753-763); this is intentional but breaks typical fairness model\n\n### 8.4 Observability and Metrics\n\n**Core metrics tracked**:\n\n| Metric | Meaning | Location |\n|--------|---------|----------|\n| `totRequestsWaiting` | Requests in queues | types.go:129 |\n| `totRequestsExecuting` | Requests executing | types.go:135 |\n| `totSeatsInUse` | Seat-seconds in use | types.go:143 |\n| `totSeatsWaiting` | Seat-seconds queued | types.go:147 |\n| `totRequestsDispatched` | Total dispatches | types.go:154 |\n| `totRequestsRejected` | Total rejections | types.go:158 |\n| `totRequestsCancelled` | Timeouts/cancellations | types.go:166 |\n| `currentR` | Virtual time | types.go:119 |\n\n**Exported via metrics** (`metrics/metrics.go`):\n- `AddRequestsInQueues()` - waiting request count\n- `AddRequestsExecuting()` - executing count\n- `AddSeatsInQueues()` - seat demand in queues\n- `AddSeatConcurrencyInUse()` - seat demand executing\n- `SetDispatchMetrics()` - virtual time info\n- `AddEpochAdvance()` - R overflow tracking\n\n**Debugging via Dump**:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n```\n\nReturns snapshot of all internal state (line 996-1015), used by debug endpoints.\n\n### 8.5 Troubleshooting Guide\n\n#### Symptom: High rejection rate\n\n**Possible causes**:\n1. ConcurrencyLimit too low for actual load\n2. QueueLengthLimit too small, queues filling up too fast\n3. Work estimator producing estimates too large, reducing usable concurrency\n\n**Investigation**:\n- Check `metrics.apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` by rejection reason\n- If \"queue-full\": increase QueueLengthLimit or NumQueues in PriorityLevelConfiguration\n- If \"concurrency-limit\": increase ConcurrencyLimit or redirect load to higher-priority flows\n\n#### Symptom: Requests not making progress (stuck in queue)\n\n**Possible causes**:\n1. Context timeout on waiting request\n2. Concurrency limit consumed by long-running requests\n3. Virtual time not advancing (bug or clock issue)\n\n**Investigation**:\n- Check `metrics.apiserver_flowcontrol_wait_duration_seconds` histogram\n- Use Dump() to see which queues have requests waiting\n- Check virtual time via `SetCurrentR` metric (should increase monotonically)\n\n#### Symptom: One flow starving others\n\n**Possible causes**:\n1. Shuffle sharding not effective (flow's requests distributed to same queue)\n2. Work estimate too small for that flow's requests\n3. Flow has higher priority level or larger nominal shares\n\n**Investigation**:\n- Check queue depths via Dump()\n- Verify shuffle sharding was enabled (DesiredNumQueues > 1)\n- Adjust DistinguisherMethod to better separate the flow\n\n---\n\n## 9. Concurrency Allocation and Multi-Level Coordination\n\n### 9.1 Integration with APF Controller\n\nThe APF controller (`apf_controller.go`) coordinates multiple QueueSets, one per non-exempt PriorityLevel:\n\n```\nAPF Controller\n├─ PriorityLevelState (per PLC)\n│  ├─ queues: QueueSet  ← Focus of this analysis\n│  ├─ pl: PriorityLevelConfiguration\n│  └─ quiescing, numPending state\n└─ FlowSchema matching logic\n```\n\n### 9.2 Concurrency Limit Allocation\n\n**Problem**: Total concurrency across all priority levels must not exceed server limit.\n\n**Solution** (`conc_alloc.go`): `computeConcurrencyAllocation()` solves a constrained optimization problem\n\n```\nInputs:\n- Total server concurrency limit C\n- Each PLC has: NominalConcurrencyShares, LendablePercent, BorrowingLimitPercent\n\nOutput:\n- Allocation vector where:\n  - sum(allocs) = C\n  - Each alloc[i] respects bounds and fairness\n```\n\n**Algorithm** (`conc_alloc.go:119-237`):\n\nUses a waterfilling algorithm: start with minimum allocations, gradually increase fairness proportion until constrained by bounds.\n\n**Key insight**: Some PLCs may be upper-bounded (can't use more) or lower-bounded (must get at least). The algorithm finds the unique allocation vector respecting all constraints.\n\n### 9.3 Borrowing and Lending\n\n**Feature**: Priority levels can temporarily borrow concurrency from others.\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `LendablePercent`: How much a PLC is willing to lend\n- `BorrowingLimitPercent`: Maximum a PLC can borrow\n\n**Implementation**: Handled at controller level; QueueSet just receives its `ConcurrencyLimit` from the controller\n\n**Implication for QueueSet**: Concurrency limit may change dynamically as other PLCs' load changes. QueueSet is agnostic; it just dispatches up to the current limit.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Critical Code Path Summary\n\n### Request Arrival to Dispatch (Fast Path, ~100 microseconds)\n\n```\napf_filter.Handle()\n  ├─ cfgCtlr.startRequest()  [classify]\n  │   ├─ Match FlowSchema: O(n) over flow schemas\n  │   ├─ Compute distinguisher hash: O(1)\n  │   └─ plState.queues.StartRequest()\n  │\n  ├─ qs.StartRequest()  [enqueue or execute]\n  │   ├─ qs.lockAndSyncTime()  [update virtual time]\n  │   ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()  [select queue]\n  │   └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  [dispatch loop]\n  │       └─ while waiting AND capacity:\n  │           └─ dispatchLocked()  [find minimum VFT queue]\n  │\n  └─ req.Finish(execFn)\n      └─ execFn()  [actual request handler]\n```\n\n### Request Completion (Cleanup Path, ~10 microseconds)\n\n```\nreq.Finish() returns\n  └─ finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n      ├─ finishRequestLocked()\n      │   ├─ Update queue.nextDispatchR (adjustment by actual service time)\n      │   ├─ Schedule deferred release if AdditionalLatency > 0\n      │   └─ removeQueueIfEmptyLocked()\n      │\n      └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  [dispatch next]\n```\n\n---\n\n## 11. Critical Files Map\n\n### QueueSet Core\n\n| File | Purpose | Lines |\n|------|---------|-------|\n| `queueset/queueset.go` | Main implementation: virtual time, dispatch, enqueue | 1030 lines |\n| `queueset/types.go` | Data structures: request, queue, queueSet | 219 lines |\n| `queueset/fifo_list.go` | FIFO list implementation with work tracking | 180 lines |\n| `queueset/doc.go` | Algorithm documentation and WFQ explanation | 120 lines |\n\n### APF Integration\n\n| File | Purpose | Lines |\n|------|---------|-------|\n| `apf_controller.go` | Config management, FlowSchema/PLC matching, concurrency allocation | 1163+ lines |\n| `apf_filter.go` | HTTP filter entry point, Handle() implementation | 204+ lines |\n| `conc_alloc.go` | Concurrency allocation solver (waterfilling algorithm) | 310+ lines |\n| `fairqueuing/interface.go` | Public interfaces: QueueSet, Request, Config | 142 lines |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/` | Entire package (queueset implementation) | ~2000 lines |\n\n### Metrics and Observability\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `metrics/metrics.go` | Metric definitions and observations |\n| `debug/` | Debug structures for Dump() output |\n\n### Testing\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `queueset/queueset_test.go` | Unit tests for QueueSet |\n| `controller_test.go` | APF controller tests |\n| `apf_filter_test.go` | Filter integration tests |\n\n---\n\n## 12. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem is a carefully engineered fair queuing implementation that adapts classical weighted fair queuing to the constraints of server request handling. Its architecture balances:\n\n- **Fairness**: Virtual time ordering ensures requests make progress proportional to their work\n- **Isolation**: Shuffle sharding prevents one bad flow from blocking others\n- **Scalability**: O(log n) per-request operations with minimal memory overhead\n- **Observability**: Rich metrics and dump capabilities for operational visibility\n- **Extensibility**: Multiple hooks for testing and customization\n\nKey design decisions—estimated service time, additional latency phases, anti-windup adjustments, and epoch advancement—collectively enable predictable, fair request handling under load.\n\n**For operators**: Focus on sizing `NumQueues` (≥8 for isolation), `QueueLengthLimit` (prevent memory bloat), and monitoring reject rates by reason. Fairness is built-in; configuration is the main lever.\n\n**For developers**: The QueueSet interface is simple (StartRequest + Finish), but the fair queuing math underneath is subtle.
