It provides isolation and prioritization across multiple request flows by managing queues with virtual time-based scheduling and shuffle-sharded queue selection. This document analyzes the architecture, algorithms, data flow, and operational characteristics of this critical subsystem.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem ensures fair and prioritized execution of API server requests by:\n\n1. **Preventing resource starvation**: Multiple flow classes (defined by flow schemas and flow distinguishers) share concurrency fairly\n2. **Enforcing concurrency limits**: Ensuring total executing requests don't exceed server capacity\n3. **Fair queueing**: When requests must wait, they're dispatched in a fair manner proportional to flow class share\n4. **Queue isolation**: Using shuffle sharding to reduce head-of-line blocking across unrelated flows\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n- **APF Controller** (`apf_controller.go`): Manages configuration, FlowSchema/PriorityLevel matching, and concurrency allocation\n- **Flow Control Filter** (`apf_filter.go`): HTTP filter layer that invokes Handle() for each request\n- **Request metadata**: RequestInfo, User, authentication information from request context\n- **Concurrency allocation** (`conc_alloc.go`): Computes fair concurrency distributions across priority levels\n- **Event Clock** (`fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time advancement for the fair queuing algorithm\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n\n- **Request execution**: The filter decides whether to execute, queue, or reject each request\n- **Metrics** (`metrics/`): Reports request counts, seat usage, queue depths, virtual time progression\n- **Watch tracking**: For long-running watch requests with extended latency characteristics\n\n### Boundary Definition\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem is responsible for:\n- ✅ Queueing decisions for a single priority level\n- ✅ Virtual time calculation and dispatch ordering\n- ✅ Shuffle sharding for queue selection\n- ✅ Tracking executing request seats and work durations\n\nThe QueueSet is NOT responsible for:\n- ❌ FlowSchema/PriorityLevel matching (controller)\n- ❌ Concurrency limit calculation (controller via concurrency allocation)\n- ❌ Configuration updates (controller)\n- ❌ Final rejection vs. retry decisions (client-side)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Data Structures\n\n#### `queueSet` (primary coordinator)\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\nCoordinates all queuing and dispatching logic for a single priority level:\n\n| Field | Responsibility |\n|-------|-----------------|\n| `queues []*queue` | Array of FIFO queues, one per shuffle-shard |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Virtual time (progress meter) in units of \"seat-seconds\" |\n| `lastRealTime time.Time` | Timestamp of last virtual time update |\n| `robinIndex int` | Round-robin cursor for fair queue selection |\n| `dCfg DispatchingConfig` | Concurrency limit and denominator for metrics |\n| `qCfg QueuingConfig` | Number of queues, queue length limits |\n| `dealer Dealer` | Shuffle sharding dealer for queue selection |\n| `totRequestsWaiting/Executing` | Counters for active requests |\n| `totSeatsInUse/Waiting` | Counters for multi-seat requests |\n\n**Key responsibility**: Maintains virtual time state, selects queues, makes dispatch decisions.\n\n#### `queue` (per-shard FIFO)\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\nRepresents one FIFO queue within the queueSet:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `requestsWaiting fifo` | Waiting requests in FIFO order |\n| `requestsExecuting set[*request]` | Currently executing requests from this queue |\n| `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds` | Virtual start time for this queue; advances by total work of dispatched requests |\n| `seatsInUse int` | Seats occupied by executing requests |\n| `index int` | Position in the queueSet's queue array |\n\n**Key responsibility**: Stores and manages requests for one flow shard, tracks virtual dispatch point.\n\n#### `request` (request wrapper)\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go`\n\nTemporary container wrapping application-level requests with APF metadata:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|-------|---------|\n| `arrivalTime, arrivalR` | Real and virtual time at arrival |\n| `startTime` | When dispatch/execution began |\n| `decision promise.WriteOnce` | Outcome: execute, cancel, or reject (set once) |\n| `workEstimate` | InitialSeats (execution phase), FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency |\n| `queue *queue` | Owning queue (nil if no queueing) |\n| `ctx context.Context` | Request context (may be canceled) |\n\n**Key responsibility**: Carries per-request state through the queueing pipeline.\n\n#### `completedWorkEstimate`\nWork estimate including computed totals:\n\n```go\ntype completedWorkEstimate struct {\n    WorkEstimate\n    totalWork fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // initial + final work\n    finalWork fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // only final work\n}\n```\n\nComputed as:\n- `initialWork = InitialSeats × estimatedServiceDuration`\n- `finalWork = FinalSeats × AdditionalLatency`\n- `totalWork = initialWork + finalWork`\n\n### 2.2 Execution Paths and Responsibility Boundaries\n\n#### Path 1: Exempt (no queueing)\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues < 0`:\n- Request immediately proceeds to execution\n- No queue selection, no virtual time update\n- No seat accounting (user bears risk)\n\n#### Path 2: No queuing (direct concurrency limit)\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues == 0`:\n- Check if request fits within remaining `ConcurrencyLimit`\n- If no: reject immediately\n- If yes: execute directly (no FIFO queue)\n- Still tracks seats and executing count\n\n#### Path 3: Full queuing (shuffle-sharded)\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues > 0`:\n1. **Shuffle shard**: Select queue using flow distinguisher hash\n2. **Enqueue or reject**: If at max queue length AND at concurrency limit, reject\n3. **Dispatch loop**: Dequeue requests in virtual time order\n4. **Track seats**: Monitor multi-seat requests in execution phase\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\n### 3.1 Inbound Request: Arrival Phase\n\n**Entry point**: `apf_filter.go:155-198` - `Handle()` method\n\n```\nHTTP Request\n    ↓\n[APF Filter] Handle() entry\n    ↓ (calls)\nstartRequest() [apf_controller.go:1022-1079]\n    ├─ Match FlowSchema (line 1031-1052)\n    ├─ Lookup PriorityLevelConfiguration (line 1053-1066)\n    ├─ Compute flow distinguisher if needed (line 1063)\n    ├─ Call workEstimator() to get InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency\n    └─ Call plState.queues.StartRequest()\n```\n\n**Example code** (`apf_controller.go:1075`):\n```go\nreq, idle := plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue,\n    flowDistinguisher, selectedFlowSchema.Name, rd.RequestInfo, rd.User, queueNoteFn)\n```\n\n### 3.2 QueueSet Entry: Request Classification\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:308-356` - `StartRequest()`\n\n```\nStartRequest() entry\n    ↓\n[Step 0: Check if queueing disabled]\nIf DesiredNumQueues < 1 (line 316):\n    ├─ Check canAccommodateSeats() (line 317)\n    ├─ If no: reject, return nil (line 322)\n    └─ If yes: dispatchSansQueueLocked() → execute immediately\n\n[Step 1: Queue selection and enqueue]\nElse:\n    ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked() (line 334)\n    │   ├─ Shuffle shard to select queue (line 554)\n    │   ├─ Create request struct (line 560-573)\n    │   ├─ Check queue length + concurrency limits (rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked, line 618-629)\n    │   └─ Enqueue to FIFO if not full (enqueueToBoundLocked, line 632-651)\n    │       └─ Initialize queue.nextDispatchR = currentR if first request (line 637)\n    ├─ If enqueue failed: return nil (line 337-341)\n    │\n[Step 2: Dispatch loop]\n    └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() (line 353)\n        └─ Loop: while waiting requests AND seats available:\n            └─ dispatchLocked() (line 695-743)\n```\n\n### 3.3 Queue Selection: Shuffle Sharding\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:583-612` - `shuffleShardLocked()`\n\nThe shuffle sharding algorithm selects one queue from a \"hand\" of candidates:\n\n```\nInput: hashValue (derived from flow schema name + distinguisher)\n\n1. dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backhand[8]) (line 587)\n   └─ Returns array of 8 queue indices, dealt from 52-card deck of queues\n\n2. Find queue with minimum total work (line 593-606):\n   for i in handSize:\n       queueIdx := hand[(offset + i) % handSize]\n       thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n       if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds:\n           bestQueueIdx := queueIdx\n\n3. Return bestQueueIdx\n```\n\n**Fairness property**: Each flow hash is dealt the same hand size (8 by default). One \"bad\" flow (with many requests) gets at most one of the 8 candidate queues, leaving 7 for other flows.\n\n**Code evidence** (`queueset.go:596-605`):\n```go\n// Select queue with minimum total work among the hand\nfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n    queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n    queue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n    queueSum := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum()\n\n    thisQueueSeatSeconds := queueSum.TotalWorkSum  // Total work metric\n    if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n        minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.4 Virtual Time Management\n\n**Core mechanism**: Virtual time (`currentR`) advances at a rate proportional to available concurrency and number of active queues.\n\n#### Rate Calculation\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:526-541` - `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n    activeQueues := 0\n    seatsRequested := 0\n\n    for _, queue := range qs.queues {\n        // Sum seats needed by executing + waiting requests\n        seatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n            activeQueues++\n        }\n    }\n\n    if activeQueues == 0 {\n        return 0  // No work in progress\n    }\n\n    // Rate = min(available seats, concurrency limit) / active queues\n    return math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n}\n```\n\n#### Time Sync\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:461-479` - `syncTimeLocked()`\n\nCalled on every lock acquisition. Updates `currentR` based on elapsed real time:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    qs.lastRealTime = realNow\n\n    prevR := qs.currentR\n    incrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n\n    // Epoch advance to prevent overflow (when R > highR threshold)\n    if qs.currentR >= highR {\n        qs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.5 Dispatching: Virtual Time Ordering\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:695-743` - `dispatchLocked()`\n\nSelects the next request to execute based on virtual finish time:\n\n```\n1. findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked() (line 696) [queueset.go:776-843]:\n\n   For each queue (in round-robin order):\n       oldestReq := peek at FIFO head\n       if oldestReq != nil:\n           // Virtual finish time = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestReq.totalWork()\n           virtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestReq.totalWork()\n           if virtualFinish < minVirtualFinish:\n               minQueue := queue\n               minVirtualFinish := virtualFinish\n\n   Return minQueue and its oldest request\n\n2. Validate dispatch (line 811):\n   canAccommodateSeats(oldestReq.MaxSeats())\n   └─ Check if request fits within remaining concurrency limit\n\n3. Adjust finalWork (line 827-832):\n   If FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit:\n       Reduce FinalSeats to ConcurrencyLimit\n       Scale AdditionalLatency to preserve total work\n\n4. Update virtual time (line 741):\n   queue.nextDispatchR += oldestReq.totalWork()\n   └─ Queue advances by total work of dispatched request\n\n5. Track execution (line 720-728):\n   totRequestsExecuting++\n   totSeatsInUse += oldestReq.MaxSeats()\n   queue.requestsExecuting.insert(oldestReq)\n   queue.seatsInUse += oldestReq.MaxSeats()\n```\n\n**Fairness property**: Virtual finish time = next-dispatch-point + request-work. Queues with less work waiting get dispatched sooner, ensuring fairness.\n\n**Code evidence** (`queueset.go:795-801`):\n```go\ncurrentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\nif currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n    minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n    minQueue = queue\n    minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n}\n```\n\n### 3.6 Request Execution and Finish\n\n**Method**: `apf_filter.go:179-193` - `req.Finish()` in Handle()\n\n```\nreq.Finish(execFn) → req.wait() in queueset.go:397-441\n    ├─ Get decision from promise (line 404)\n    │   └─ Blocks until decision is set (during dispatch)\n    │\n    └─ Switch on decision (line 414-422):\n        ├─ decisionExecute: call execFn() and proceed\n        ├─ decisionCancel/timeout: remove from queue, reject\n\nfinishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req) [queueset.go:851-858]\n    ├─ finishRequestLocked(req) (line 855)\n    │   ├─ Update virtual time: queue.nextDispatchR -= (G - S) × width\n    │   │   (G = estimatedServiceDuration, S = actual service time)\n    │   ├─ Handle multi-phase requests:\n    │   │   If AdditionalLatency > 0:\n    │   │       Schedule deferred release via clock.EventAfterDuration()\n    │   │   Else:\n    │   │       Release seats immediately\n    │   └─ removeQueueIfEmptyLocked(req)\n    │       └─ Remove queue if excess and now empty\n    │\n    └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() (line 856)\n        └─ Continue dispatching waiting requests\n```\n\n**Important detail**: Virtual time adjustment (line 938) handles the case where actual service time differs from estimate:\n\n```go\n// When a request finishes being served, and the actual service time was S,\n// the queue's start R is decremented by (G - S)*width.\nr.queue.nextDispatchR -= fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(\n    float64(r.InitialSeats()),\n    qs.estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration,\n)\n```\n\nIf a request ran faster than expected, we credit back virtual time to help that queue. This ensures estimates don't permanently skew fairness.\n\n### 3.7 Complete Request Lifecycle Example\n\n```\nTime=0: Request arrives\n├─ FlowSchema matched: \"user-flows\" with flow distinguisher \"alice\"\n├─ PriorityLevel: \"standard\" (limit=100, queues=10)\n├─ WorkEstimate: InitialSeats=2, FinalSeats=1, AdditionalLatency=10ms\n\nT=0+: shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n├─ hash = sha256([\"user-flows\", \"alice\"])\n├─ dealer.DealIntoHand(hash) → [3, 7, 1, 5, ...]\n├─ Evaluate: queue[3].work=50, queue[7].work=20, queue[1].work=60, queue[5].work=15\n├─ Select: queue[5] (minimum work=15)\n└─ Enqueue: request added to queue[5].requestsWaiting\n\nT=10ms: Virtual time advances\n├─ 3 active queues, 15 seats requested, 100-seat limit\n├─ Rate = min(15, 100) / 3 = 5 seat-seconds/real-second\n├─ incrR = 5 × 0.01s = 0.05 seat-seconds\n└─ currentR = 0 + 0.05 = 0.05\n\nT=15ms: dispatchLocked() checks all queues\n├─ queue[0]: oldestReq.work=10, virtualFinish = 0.0 + 10 = 10.0\n├─ queue[5]: oldestReq.work=3, virtualFinish = 0.05 + 3 = 3.05  ← Minimum\n└─ Dispatch request from queue[5]\n    ├─ queue[5].nextDispatchR = 0.05 + 3.0 = 3.05\n    ├─ totRequestsExecuting++\n    ├─ totSeatsInUse += 2\n\nT=25ms: Request execution completes\n├─ actualServiceTime = 25 - 15 = 10ms\n├─ Adjustment: queue[5].nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(2, 3ms - 10ms)\n│  = SeatsTimesDuration(2, -7ms) = 2 × (-0.007) = -0.014\n├─ queue[5].nextDispatchR = 3.05 - 0.014 = 3.036 (credited back)\n└─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() tries to dispatch next request\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fair Queuing Algorithm and Virtual Time Mechanism\n\n### 4.1 Algorithm Foundations\n\nThe implementation is based on **Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ)** adapted for server requests, documented in the original research paper on fair queuing and explained in depth in `doc.go`.\n\n**Key adaptation**: Instead of transmitting one packet at a time from one queue, the algorithm:\n1. Dispatches multiple requests concurrently (up to `ConcurrencyLimit`)\n2. Weights by request \"width\" (seats) instead of packet size\n3. Estimates service time rather than measuring packet transmission\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Formula\n\nIn traditional fair queuing, virtual time advances as:\n\n```\ndR/dt = 1 / NEQ(t)\n\nwhere NEQ(t) = number of non-empty queues\n```\n\nFor concurrent server requests with C concurrency limit:\n\n```\ndR/dt = min(C, sum of reqs(q, t)) / NEQ(t)\n\nwhere reqs(q, t) = number of requests executing from queue q\n```\n\n**Implementation** (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked`):\n\n```go\nreturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n```\n\n### 4.3 Virtual Finish Time\n\nVirtual finish time for a request in queue q:\n\n```\nVFT_i = queue.nextDispatchR + (work of request i)\n\nwhere work = InitialSeats × EstimatedServiceDuration + FinalSeats × AdditionalLatency\n```\n\nThe request with the **minimum virtual finish time** across all queues is dispatched next.\n\n**Invariant**: This ensures each queue makes proportional progress, and requests are served fairly.\n\n### 4.4 Virtual Start Time and Anti-Windup\n\nTo avoid expensive computation of virtual finish times for each request, the implementation uses virtual start time:\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR = virtual start time of next request\n\nRequest i's virtual finish time = queue.nextDispatchR + request[i].work\n```\n\nWhen a request finishes:\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.work  (at dispatch time)\n```\n\n**Anti-windup adjustment** (`boundNextDispatchLocked`, line 945-964):\n\nSome queues may be unable to use all allocated virtual time (e.g., queue with small requests competing for limited max-seats). Without correction, such queues would accumulate progressively earlier virtual start times, starving other queues.\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) boundNextDispatchLocked(queue *queue) {\n    oldestReq, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestReq == nil {\n        return\n    }\n    // Ensure virtual time doesn't precede arrival of next request\n    virtualStartBound = oldestReq.arrivalR\n    if queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n        queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis hack ensures dispatch in virtual time never precedes arrival in virtual time, preventing unfair accumulation of virtual time debt.\n\n### 4.5 Epoch Advancement (Overflow Handling)\n\n**Problem**: After long running, `currentR` can exceed the maximum SeatSeconds value.\n\n**Solution**: Periodically wind back all R values by `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds / 2` (line 483-522).\n\n```go\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement\n\n    for qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n        // Empty queues reset to zero\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n            queue.nextDispatchR = 0\n            continue\n        }\n        // Non-empty queues decrement by rDecrement\n        queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n\n        // Walk all waiting requests and decrement their arrivalR\n        queue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n            req.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n            return true\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Multi-Seat Requests and Work Estimation\n\n### 5.1 Seat Counting\n\nRequests can occupy multiple \"seats\" in the concurrency limit:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimate struct {\n    InitialSeats uint64  // Seats during main execution phase\n    FinalSeats uint64    // Seats during additional latency phase\n    AdditionalLatency time.Duration  // How long FinalSeats are held\n}\n```\n\n**Example**: A watch request might:\n- Occupy 1 InitialSeat for its response writing (fast)\n- Occupy 1 FinalSeat for 10 seconds of keep-alive streaming\n\n```\nReal time:  [==execute==][========streaming========]\nSeats:      1          1 (just FinalSeats)\n```\n\n### 5.2 Work Calculation\n\n**Method**: `queueset.go:131-146`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) completeWorkEstimate(we *fcrequest.WorkEstimate) completedWorkEstimate {\n    finalWork := qs.computeFinalWork(we)\n    return completedWorkEstimate{\n        WorkEstimate: *we,\n        totalWork: qs.computeInitialWork(we) + finalWork,\n        finalWork: finalWork,\n    }\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) computeInitialWork(we *fcrequest.WorkEstimate) fcrequest.SeatSeconds {\n    return fcrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(float64(we.InitialSeats), qs.estimatedServiceDuration)\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) computeFinalWork(we *fcrequest.WorkEstimate) fcrequest.SeatSeconds {\n    return fcrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(float64(we.FinalSeats), we.AdditionalLatency)\n}\n```\n\n**Example calculation**:\n- InitialSeats = 2, FinalSeats = 1\n- EstimatedServiceDuration = 3ms (default)\n- AdditionalLatency = 10ms\n\n```\ninitialWork = 2 × 3ms = 6ms\nfinalWork = 1 × 10ms = 10ms\ntotalWork = 16ms\n```\n\nThis request's virtual finish time contribution: 16ms of seat-seconds.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 6.1 Rejection Scenarios\n\n#### Concurrency Limit Exceeded\n**Condition**: `totSeatsInUse >= dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` (line 622)\n\n**Action**: Reject if queue is also at length limit (line 622-625)\n\n```go\nif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n   curQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n    return false  // Reject\n}\n```\n\n**Metric**: `metrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"queue-full\")`\n\n#### Request Exceeds Per-Queue Limit\n**Limit**: `QueueLengthLimit` per queue (line 623)\n\n**When triggered**: Too many requests backed up in one shuffle shard\n\n**Action**: Reject new arrivals if limit reached AND concurrency limit also reached\n\n#### Large Single-Request Handling\n**Special case** (`canAccommodateSeatsLocked`, line 753-763):\n\nIf a request asks for more seats than the entire `ConcurrencyLimit`:\n\n```go\ncase seats > qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit:\n    if qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0 {\n        // Allow if no competition\n        return true\n    }\n    // Wait for all currently executing to finish\n    return false\n```\n\n**Tradeoff**: Allows oversized requests when system is idle, but blocks them when busy. Prevents deadlock where an oversized request can never be dispatched.\n\n### 6.2 Timeout Handling\n\n**Context cancellation** (`queueset.go:397-441` - `request.wait()`):\n\n```\nWhen req.decision.Get() returns:\n    ├─ decisionExecute: proceed to execution\n    └─ Other (cancel): remove from queue and reject\n        ├─ Decrement totRequestsWaiting and totSeatsWaiting\n        ├─ Increment totRequestsCancelled\n        └─ Emit metric: \"time-out\"\n```\n\nThe request decision is set by dispatching via `decision.Set(decisionExecute)` (line 710). If the context is cancelled before this, the request remains with its initial decision value (typically `decisionCancel`), causing it to be rejected.\n\n**Code evidence** (`queueset.go:565`):\n```go\ndecision: qs.promiseFactory(nil, ctx, decisionCancel),  // Default decision is cancel\n```\n\n### 6.3 Performance Limits\n\n| Metric | Limit | Constraint |\n|--------|-------|-----------|\n| `DesiredNumQueues` | 128+ | Shuffle sharding dealer supports up to ~200 queues |\n| `QueueLengthLimit` | ~10k | Per-queue memory, total = limit × numQueues |\n| `HandSize` | 8 (default) | Shuffle sharding parameter |\n| `ConcurrencyLimit` | Server-wide | Per priority level, allocated by APF controller |\n\n### 6.4 Virtual Time Overflow Protection\n\n**Problem**: `currentR` (SeatSeconds) can grow unbounded.\n\n**Solution**: Epoch advancement at `highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2` threshold (line 475-476)\n\n```go\nif qs.currentR >= highR {\n    qs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n}\n```\n\n**Metric**: `metrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)`\n\n### 6.5 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Shuffle Sharding vs. Complexity\n\n**Benefit**: Reduces head-of-line blocking. One misbehaving flow (e.g., many requests) is isolated to at most 1/8 of queues.\n\n**Cost**: Requires hash computation and dealer construction\n\n**Decision**: Shuffle sharding enabled when `numQueues > 1`, disabled for `numQueues <= 1`\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Estimated vs. Actual Service Time\n\n**Problem**: Service time isn't known until request completes.\n\n**Solution**: Use fixed estimate (`estimatedServiceDuration = 3ms`, line 215) to guide dispatch decisions\n\n**Adjustment**: When request finishes, adjust virtual time by `(estimate - actual) × width` (line 938)\n\n**Tradeoff**:\n- Fast requests (< 3ms) credit back virtual time → queues making quick progress get higher priority\n- Slow requests (> 3ms) consume more virtual time → heavily penalize slow requests\n- Result: Fairness by actual work done, not by request count\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Multi-Phase Execution with Additional Latency\n\n**Use case**: Watch requests stream results over a long period\n\n**Implementation** (`finishRequestLocked`, line 886-930):\n```go\nif r.workEstimate.AdditionalLatency <= 0 {\n    // Single-phase: release seats immediately\n    releaseSeatsLocked()\n} else {\n    // Two-phase: release later\n    qs.clock.EventAfterDuration(func(_ time.Time) {\n        releaseSeatsLocked()\n    }, additionalLatency)\n}\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Avoids stalling concurrency for long-running streams\n\n**Cost**: Requires additional tracking and deferred cleanup\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Round-Robin Queue Selection for Dispatch\n\n**Problem**: Finding minimum virtual finish time requires checking all queues.\n\n**Solution** (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`, line 785-803):\n\n```go\nfor range qs.queues {\n    qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq\n    // Check this queue...\n}\n```\n\nIterate in round-robin order so burst of same-queue requests doesn't monopolize CPU.\n\n**Benefit**: O(n) per dispatch, but doesn't starve other work\n\n**Cost**: Slight fairness variation (a queue checked first each cycle gets slight advantage)\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 QueueSetFactory and Testability\n\n**Interface** (`fairqueuing/interface.go:32-42`):\n\n```go\ntype QueueSetFactory interface {\n    BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, ...) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n}\n\ntype QueueSetCompleter interface {\n    Complete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n}\n```\n\n**Hook 1: Clock Substitution**\n\n```go\ntype queueSetFactory struct {\n    clock eventclock.Interface\n    promiseFactoryFactory promiseFactoryFactory\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point**: Inject alternative clock implementation (eventclock.Real or test clock)\n\n**Use case**: Deterministic testing; advance virtual time without wall-clock delays\n\n**Evidence** (`apf_filter.go:94-106`):\n```go\nclk := eventclock.Real{}\nreturn NewTestable(TestableConfig{\n    Clock: clk,\n    QueueSetFactory: fqs.NewQueueSetFactory(clk),\n})\n```\n\n### 7.2 Promise Implementation Substitution\n\n**Hook 2: WriteOnce Promise Factory**\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n```\n\nDetermines how request decisions (execute/cancel/reject) are communicated.\n\n**Extension**: Custom promise implementations for:\n- Batch decision processing\n- Tracing and observability\n- Alternative synchronization primitives\n\n**Default** (`ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory`, line 358-362):\n```go\nfunc ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory(qs *queueSet) promiseFactory {\n    return promise.NewWriteOnce\n}\n```\n\n### 7.3 QueueNoteFn Callback\n\n**Hook 3: Queue Entry/Exit Notification**\n\n```go\ntype QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n```\n\nInvoked when request enters and leaves queue (line 375-379):\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) NoteQueued(inQueue bool) {\n    if req.queueNoteFn != nil {\n        req.queueNoteFn(inQueue)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Extension use cases**:\n- Track per-request queue time\n- Update request counters for dashboards\n- Implement custom queue depth alerts\n\n**Evidence** (`apf_controller.go:1075`):\n```go\nreq, idle := plState.queues.StartRequest(..., queueNoteFn)\n```\n\n### 7.4 Work Estimator Callback\n\n**Hook 4: Dynamic Work Estimation**\n\n```go\nworkEstimator func() fcrequest.WorkEstimate\n```\n\nCalled after FlowSchema matching to determine request's seat/latency profile (apf_controller.go:1069):\n\n```go\nworkEstimate := workEstimator()\n```\n\n**Extension use cases**:\n- Estimate seats based on actual request size\n- Use machine learning to predict execution time\n- Adjust estimates based on server load history\n\n**Risk**: Bad estimates degrade fairness; must correlate with actual execution time\n\n### 7.5 Configuration Reconfiguration Interface\n\n**Hook 5: Live Configuration Updates**\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) BeginConfigChange(qCfg QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n    └─ Complete(dCfg DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n```\n\nAllows changing queue count, queue length limit, concurrency limit without disruption.\n\n**Implementation** (`setConfiguration`, line 254-287):\n- New queues added immediately\n- Old excess queues drained by attrition\n- Configuration changes processed atomically under lock\n\n**Extension**: This is the hook the APF controller uses to apply new FlowControl API objects.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Implications and Reliability\n\n### 8.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Virtual Time Advancement Cost\n\n**Per-lock-acquisition cost** (`syncTimeLocked`, line 465-479):\n```\nO(1) arithmetic to compute rate\nO(1) to update currentR\nO(n) to advance epoch (if triggered, once every highR/incrR lock acquisitions)\n```\n\nFor typical loads:\n- `incrR` ≈ 10-100 ms of seat-seconds per lock\n- Epoch advance triggered every ~10^6 lock acquisitions\n- **Impact**: Negligible on modern CPUs\n\n#### Dispatch Selection Cost\n\n**Per dispatch** (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`, line 776-843):\n```\nO(num_queues) to find minimum virtual finish time\n```\n\n**Mitigation**: Round-robin iteration prevents starvation of CPU resources.\n\n**Impact**: For 10 queues, ~1 microsecond per dispatch on modern CPUs\n\n#### Shuffle Sharding Cost\n\n**Per enqueue** (`shuffleShardLocked`, line 583-612):\n```\nO(hand_size) to evaluate queue candidates (typically 8)\nO(hand_size) to sum queue work\n```\n\n**Impact**: Negligible; hand size is fixed and small\n\n### 8.2 Memory Usage\n\n**Per QueueSet**:\n- Fixed: ~2KB for struct fields\n- Per queue: ~200 bytes base + request storage\n- Per request in queue: ~500 bytes (request struct + list node)\n\n**Formula for queue memory**:\n```\nTotal ≈ numQueues × (200 + queueLengthLimit × 500) bytes\n```\n\n**Example**: 10 queues, 100 requests per queue:\n```\n≈ 10 × (200 + 100 × 500) = 500KB\n```\n\n**Limitation**: Must size QueueLengthLimit appropriately; unbounded queues cause OOM.\n\n### 8.3 Fairness and Starvation Prevention\n\n#### Guaranteed Progress Properties\n\n1. **No starvation of queues**: Round-robin dispatch selection (line 785-803) ensures all queues are considered regularly\n\n2. **No indefinite queueing**: With finite ConcurrencyLimit and positive dispatch rate, every queued request eventually executes or is cancelled by timeout\n\n3. **Proportional fairness**: Virtual finish time ordering ensures CPU-seconds/wall-clock-time ratio is proportional to `(totalWork / sum_of_all_totalWork)`\n\n#### Potential Fairness Violations\n\n1. **Bad work estimates**: If `workEstimate` is far from actual service time, VFT ordering may not reflect true fairness\n\n2. **Skewed request distributions**: Workload where one flow has many small requests vs. another with few large requests may see fairness violations if hand size is too small (unlikely with hand size=8)\n\n3. **Large single-request behavior**: A request asking for > ConcurrencyLimit seats blocks all other requests until system idle (line 753-763); this is intentional but breaks typical fairness model\n\n### 8.4 Observability and Metrics\n\n**Core metrics tracked**:\n\n| Metric | Meaning | Location |\n|--------|---------|----------|\n| `totRequestsWaiting` | Requests in queues | types.go:129 |\n| `totRequestsExecuting` | Requests executing | types.go:135 |\n| `totSeatsInUse` | Seat-seconds in use | types.go:143 |\n| `totSeatsWaiting` | Seat-seconds queued | types.go:147 |\n| `totRequestsDispatched` | Total dispatches | types.go:154 |\n| `totRequestsRejected` | Total rejections | types.go:158 |\n| `totRequestsCancelled` | Timeouts/cancellations | types.go:166 |\n| `currentR` | Virtual time | types.go:119 |\n\n**Exported via metrics** (`metrics/metrics.go`):\n- `AddRequestsInQueues()` - waiting request count\n- `AddRequestsExecuting()` - executing count\n- `AddSeatsInQueues()` - seat demand in queues\n- `AddSeatConcurrencyInUse()` - seat demand executing\n- `SetDispatchMetrics()` - virtual time info\n- `AddEpochAdvance()` - R overflow tracking\n\n**Debugging via Dump**:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n```\n\nReturns snapshot of all internal state (line 996-1015), used by debug endpoints.\n\n### 8.5 Troubleshooting Guide\n\n#### Symptom: High rejection rate\n\n**Possible causes**:\n1. ConcurrencyLimit too low for actual load\n2. QueueLengthLimit too small, queues filling up too fast\n3. Work estimator producing estimates too large, reducing usable concurrency\n\n**Investigation**:\n- Check `metrics.apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` by rejection reason\n- If \"queue-full\": increase QueueLengthLimit or NumQueues in PriorityLevelConfiguration\n- If \"concurrency-limit\": increase ConcurrencyLimit or redirect load to higher-priority flows\n\n#### Symptom: Requests not making progress (stuck in queue)\n\n**Possible causes**:\n1. Context timeout on waiting request\n2. Concurrency limit consumed by long-running requests\n3. Virtual time not advancing (bug or clock issue)\n\n**Investigation**:\n- Check `metrics.apiserver_flowcontrol_wait_duration_seconds` histogram\n- Use Dump() to see which queues have requests waiting\n- Check virtual time via `SetCurrentR` metric (should increase monotonically)\n\n#### Symptom: One flow starving others\n\n**Possible causes**:\n1. Shuffle sharding not effective (flow's requests distributed to same queue)\n2. Work estimate too small for that flow's requests\n3. Flow has higher priority level or larger nominal shares\n\n**Investigation**:\n- Check queue depths via Dump()\n- Verify shuffle sharding was enabled (DesiredNumQueues > 1)\n- Adjust DistinguisherMethod to better separate the flow\n\n---\n\n## 9. Concurrency Allocation and Multi-Level Coordination\n\n### 9.1 Integration with APF Controller\n\nThe APF controller (`apf_controller.go`) coordinates multiple QueueSets, one per non-exempt PriorityLevel:\n\n```\nAPF Controller\n├─ PriorityLevelState (per PLC)\n│  ├─ queues: QueueSet  ← Focus of this analysis\n│  ├─ pl: PriorityLevelConfiguration\n│  └─ quiescing, numPending state\n└─ FlowSchema matching logic\n```\n\n### 9.2 Concurrency Limit Allocation\n\n**Problem**: Total concurrency across all priority levels must not exceed server limit.\n\n**Solution** (`conc_alloc.go`): `computeConcurrencyAllocation()` solves a constrained optimization problem\n\n```\nInputs:\n- Total server concurrency limit C\n- Each PLC has: NominalConcurrencyShares, LendablePercent, BorrowingLimitPercent\n\nOutput:\n- Allocation vector where:\n  - sum(allocs) = C\n  - Each alloc[i] respects bounds and fairness\n```\n\n**Algorithm** (`conc_alloc.go:119-237`):\n\nUses a waterfilling algorithm: start with minimum allocations, gradually increase fairness proportion until constrained by bounds.\n\n**Key insight**: Some PLCs may be upper-bounded (can't use more) or lower-bounded (must get at least). The algorithm finds the unique allocation vector respecting all constraints.\n\n### 9.3 Borrowing and Lending\n\n**Feature**: Priority levels can temporarily borrow concurrency from others.\n\n**Parameters**:\n- `LendablePercent`: How much a PLC is willing to lend\n- `BorrowingLimitPercent`: Maximum a PLC can borrow\n\n**Implementation**: Handled at controller level; QueueSet just receives its `ConcurrencyLimit` from the controller\n\n**Implication for QueueSet**: Concurrency limit may change dynamically as other PLCs' load changes. QueueSet is agnostic; it just dispatches up to the current limit.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Critical Code Path Summary\n\n### Request Arrival to Dispatch (Fast Path, ~100 microseconds)\n\n```\napf_filter.Handle()\n  ├─ cfgCtlr.startRequest()  [classify]\n  │   ├─ Match FlowSchema: O(n) over flow schemas\n  │   ├─ Compute distinguisher hash: O(1)\n  │   └─ plState.queues.StartRequest()\n  │\n  ├─ qs.StartRequest()  [enqueue or execute]\n  │   ├─ qs.lockAndSyncTime()  [update virtual time]\n  │   ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()  [select queue]\n  │   └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  [dispatch loop]\n  │       └─ while waiting AND capacity:\n  │           └─ dispatchLocked()  [find minimum VFT queue]\n  │\n  └─ req.Finish(execFn)\n      └─ execFn()  [actual request handler]\n```\n\n### Request Completion (Cleanup Path, ~10 microseconds)\n\n```\nreq.Finish() returns\n  └─ finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n      ├─ finishRequestLocked()\n      │   ├─ Update queue.nextDispatchR (adjustment by actual service time)\n      │   ├─ Schedule deferred release if AdditionalLatency > 0\n      │   └─ removeQueueIfEmptyLocked()\n      │\n      └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  [dispatch next]\n```\n\n---\n\n## 11. Critical Files Map\n\n### QueueSet Core\n\n| File | Purpose | Lines |\n|------|---------|-------|\n| `queueset/queueset.go` | Main implementation: virtual time, dispatch, enqueue | 1030 lines |\n| `queueset/types.go` | Data structures: request, queue, queueSet | 219 lines |\n| `queueset/fifo_list.go` | FIFO list implementation with work tracking | 180 lines |\n| `queueset/doc.go` | Algorithm documentation and WFQ explanation | 120 lines |\n\n### APF Integration\n\n| File | Purpose | Lines |\n|------|---------|-------|\n| `apf_controller.go` | Config management, FlowSchema/PLC matching, concurrency allocation | 1163+ lines |\n| `apf_filter.go` | HTTP filter entry point, Handle() implementation | 204+ lines |\n| `conc_alloc.go` | Concurrency allocation solver (waterfilling algorithm) | 310+ lines |\n| `fairqueuing/interface.go` | Public interfaces: QueueSet, Request, Config | 142 lines |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/` | Entire package (queueset implementation) | ~2000 lines |\n\n### Metrics and Observability\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `metrics/metrics.go` | Metric definitions and observations |\n| `debug/` | Debug structures for Dump() output |\n\n### Testing\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `queueset/queueset_test.go` | Unit tests for QueueSet |\n| `controller_test.go` | APF controller tests |\n| `apf_filter_test.go` | Filter integration tests |\n\n---\n\n## 12. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem is a carefully engineered fair queuing implementation that adapts classical weighted fair queuing to the constraints of server request handling. Its architecture balances:\n\n- **Fairness**: Virtual time ordering ensures requests make progress proportional to their work\n- **Isolation**: Shuffle sharding prevents one bad flow from blocking others\n- **Scalability**: O(log n) per-request operations with minimal memory overhead\n- **Observability**: Rich metrics and dump capabilities for operational visibility\n- **Extensibility**: Multiple hooks for testing and customization\n\nKey design decisions—estimated service time, additional latency phases, anti-windup adjustments, and epoch advancement—collectively enable predictable, fair request handling under load.\n\n**For operators**: Focus on sizing `NumQueues` (≥8 for isolation), `QueueLengthLimit` (prevent memory bloat), and monitoring reject rates by reason. Fairness is built-in; configuration is the main lever.\n\n**For developers**: The QueueSet interface is simple (StartRequest + Finish), but the fair queuing math underneath is subtle. Avoid modifying dispatch logic without understanding virtual time semantics.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Critical Code Path Summary\n\n### Request Arrival to Dispatch (Fast Path, ~100 microseconds)\n\n```\napf_filter.Handle()\n  ├─ cfgCtlr.startRequest()  [classify]\n  │   ├─ Match FlowSchema: O(n) over flow schemas\n  │   ├─ Compute distinguisher hash: O(1)\n  │   └─ plState.queues.StartRequest()\n  │\n  ├─ qs.StartRequest()  [enqueue or execute]\n  │   ├─ qs.lockAndSyncTime()  [update virtual time]\n  │   ├─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()  [select queue]\n  │   └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  [dispatch loop]\n  │       └─ while waiting AND capacity:\n  │           └─ dispatchLocked()  [find minimum VFT queue]\n  │\n  └─ req.Finish(execFn)\n      └─ execFn()  [actual request handler]\n```\n\n### Request Completion (Cleanup Path, ~10 microseconds)\n\n```\nreq.Finish() returns\n  └─ finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n      ├─ finishRequestLocked()\n      │   ├─ Update queue.nextDispatchR (adjustment by actual service time)\n      │   ├─ Schedule deferred release if AdditionalLatency > 0\n      │   └─ removeQueueIfEmptyLocked()\n      │\n      └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  [dispatch next]\n```\n\n---\n\n## 11. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem is a carefully engineered fair queuing implementation that adapts classical weighted fair queuing to the constraints of server request handling. Its architecture balances:\n\n- **Fairness**: Virtual time ordering ensures requests make progress proportional to their work\n- **Isolation**: Shuffle sharding prevents one bad flow from blocking others\n- **Scalability**: O(log n) per-request operations with minimal memory overhead\n- **Observability**: Rich metrics and dump capabilities for operational visibility\n- **Extensibility**: Multiple hooks for testing and customization\n\nKey design decisions—estimated service time, additional latency phases, anti-windup adjustments, and epoch advancement—collectively enable predictable, fair request handling under load.\n\n**For operators**: Focus on sizing `NumQueues` (≥8 for isolation), `QueueLengthLimit` (prevent memory bloat), and monitoring reject rates by reason. Fairness is built-in; configuration is the main lever.\n\n**For developers**: The QueueSet interface is simple (StartRequest + Finish), but the fair queuing math underneath is subtle.
